THE
INDIA
OFFICE LIST

A rectangular stamp with a double border. Inside, the text reads "INDIA OFFICE" at the top, "20 JUN. 1918" in the middle, and "LIBRARY." at the bottom.

FOR

1918

COMPILED FROM OFFICIAL RECORDS BY DIRECTION OF THE
SECRETARY OF STATE FOR INDIA IN COUNCIL.

An oval-shaped stamp. The text "INDIA OFFICE" is curved along the top inner edge, and "LIBRARY" is curved along the bottom inner edge. There are two small dots on the left and right sides of the oval.

LONDON:
HARRISON AND SONS, 45, PALL MALL,
BOOKSELLERS TO HIS MAJESTY AND H.R.H. THE PRINCE OF WALES

1918.

Price Fifteen Shillings net.

P R E F A C E.

IN the lists of Officers serving in India, which are contained in pages 5 to 119 of this volume, only substantive appointments are, as a rule, shown; and, except in the case of members of the Indian Civil Service, the names of Officers drawing substantive pay of less than Rs. 500 a month are not included. The names shown in italics are those of Officers who are in foreign service, super-numerary, seconded, or employed outside their own departments.

To meet the difficulty that arises from the lack of uniformity in India in the use of surnames, Indian names are in doubtful cases twice indexed, and cross references are made in the Record of Services. Rulers of States are shown under the names of their States.

The principle of selection followed in the Record of Services (pages 425 to 742) is explained on page 423.

The "Index of Subjects and Appointments" is on pages iv to xviii, and the "Index of Names" on pages 749 to 806. Names in the Honours Lists and Record of Services are shown in the Index of Names by "A" and "B," with a note prefixed referring to the Alphabetical Lists on pages 171 to 189 and pages 425 to 742.

It is requested that intimations or errors in the lists, or of omissions, may be addressed to the Editor of the India Office List, India Office, Whitehall, London, S.W.

May, 1918.

INDIAN TROOP SERVICE.

The business of the Troop Service is conducted by Rear-Admiral Herbert W. Savory, M.V.O., Director of Transports at the Admiralty, acting as the Agent of the Secretary of State for India in Council.

PROBATIONERS FOR THE INDIAN FOREST SERVICE.

Probationers undergo a course of study for two or more years at Oxford, Cambridge, or Edinburgh, and on the Continent. Their training is under the superintendence of the Director of Indian Forest Studies, Mr. A. M. F. Caccia, M.V.O., M.A., of the Indian Forest Service.

INDIA OFFICE LIBRARY.

The Library was founded in 1801 by the East India Company. It contains about 100,000 printed books, principally relating to the East, and 15,000 Oriental manuscripts and xylographs. There are the following catalogues, and others are in preparation:—

ORIENTAL MANUSCRIPTS AND XYLOGRAPHS.IN PRINT.

Sanskrit.—Mackenzie Collection. H. H. Wilson. Calcutta, 1828, 2 vols.
" General Collection. J. Eggeling. London, 1888, &c.

" Hodgson Collection. Sir W. W. Hunter. (Life of B. H. Hodgson, London, 1896, p. 344.)
" Tagore Collection. S. Mohun Tagore. Calcutta, 1890.
" " " T. Aufrecht. (Zeitsch. der Deutsch. Morgenländ. Gesellschaft, lviii, pp. 525-38, 1904.)
" Böhler Collection. G. Böhler. (Zeitsch. der Deutsch. Morgenländ. Gesellschaft, xlii, pp. 530-52, 1888.)
" Royal Society Collection. C. H. Tawney and F. W. Thomas. London, 1903.
" Aufrecht Collection (MSS., Indices, Pratika-lists, &c.). F. W. Thomas. (Journal of the Royal Asiatic Society, London, 1908, pp. 1029-63.)

Arabic.—O. Loth. London, 1877.

Extract from the Rules for the use of the Library:—

  1. 1. The use of the Library (including the Reading Room) is restricted to (a) members of the establishment of the India Office, (b) persons named in the India Office List, (c) gazetted officers of the Indian Army or of the British Army in India, and (d) such other persons as have previously obtained tickets for that purpose.
  2. 2. Books can be borrowed only with the sanction of the Librarian, who shall require from each person an acknowledgment for whatever work he may be permitted to consult or take away on loan. In the case of an Oriental manuscript, the approval of the authorities must first be obtained; and, except in special cases, a bond for the safe return of the manuscript will be required.
INDIA OFFICE LIBRARY—continued.PRINTED BOOKS AND LITHOGRAPHS—continued.
  1. 3. No book thus borrowed shall be kept more than three months; but when returned, it may be borrowed again by the same reader, unless wanted by another reader, or required in the Library for any purpose. In the case, however, of scholars engaged in special investigations, it shall be in the power of the Librarian to extend the loan of any book without insisting on its being previously returned, provided that the borrower has certified in writing that the book is in good condition. No periodical shall be kept longer than one week. A work may be recalled at any time, at the discretion of the Librarian.
  2. 4. The Library is generally open on ordinary weekdays from 10 a.m. to 5 p.m., and on Saturdays till 1 p.m. It is closed on Good Friday and the day following, Christmas Day, His Majesty's Birthday, and the Bank Holidays; also during one month in each year for cleaning purposes. No book or MS. will be issued less than half-an-hour before the time of closing.

1801 David Scott (e) (2nd time). Charles Mills.
1802 John Roberts (2nd time). Jacob Bosanquet (2nd time).

(a.) On the death of Mr. Boulton, the Court, on October 12, appointed Edward Wheeler, Chairman, and John Harrison, Deputy.

(b.) Afterwards Sir George Wombwell, Bart.

(c.) Sir Henry Fletcher being disqualified, the Court, on November 26, appointed Nathaniel Smith, Chairman, and on the next day, William Devaynes, Deputy.

(d.) Afterwards Sir Stephen Lushington, Bart.

(e.) Mr. Scott resigned the Chair, and, on September 2, the Court appointed Chas. Mills, Chairman, and John Roberts, Deputy.

(f.) Afterwards Sir William James, Bart.

(g.) Afterwards Sir Henry Fletcher, Bart. Mr. Gregory being disqualified, the Court, on July 31, appointed Sir Henry Fletcher, Chairman, and, the next day, Nathaniel Smith, Deputy.

(h.) William Devaynes appointed December 2, Deputy Chairman, in place of John Michie, deceased.

The Right Hon. Charles Grant (g) 6 Dec., 1830

* The Board, as established in 1784, consisted of one of the Secretaries of State, the Chancellor of the Exchequer, and not more than four other Privy Councillors. The Secretary of State was to preside, when present, and in his absence, the Chancellor of the Exchequer; in the absence of both, the senior Commissioner present was to take the chair. This system was altered in 1793, when it was enacted that the Commissioner named first in the Letters Patent was to be President.

† Date of notice in London Gazette, directing Letters Patent to be passed.
